And I have already warned you away from this one, and I saw that because of the size of the arrow and the condition of the patient's internal organs, it was clear that he would die.
And I saw another surgeon who was being paid by a duke of our land for surgery, and entrusted to a blacksmith the person with a fractured thigh; and the surgeon prepared the wound with his ignorance, extracted the fracture onto the wound with forceps and awls with great tension, and did not leave any breath in the wound.

Chapter 48.
On the Cauterization of Stupor.
If any member becomes numb or sleepy and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters, and does not heal, then you should cauterize that numb member with cauteries according to the size of the member or its smallness.
And let your cautery be a little into the flesh of the bone, And it is necessary to cover that with an ointment until it heals.
And sometimes the numbness is cauterized, which has descended to the arms and legs, and to the vertebrae of the back and chest, and to the exit of the nerves that serve that member, and the numbness is thus removed.
But do not suppose anything about this except that which is wise in the anatomy of the members and the exit of the nerves, throughout all the moving body.
Chapter 49.
On the Cauterization of Ulcers that are Morbid.
When an ulcer is old and does not respond to any of the medicated ointments, then you should cauterize over it with a red-hot cautery for a little while, according to the thickness of the flesh in that place, until the whiteness and the color are removed from it, and its color is changed.
And then cover that with a mixture of flour of barley and lentils with hot oil and leaves of marjoram, and blood of pigeon or lamb's blood, taking one part of each and mixing them together, and apply a bandage over it until it heals.
Chapter 50.
On the Cauterization of Boils.
When a boil is beginning and you want to burst it, then you should cauterize that with a circular cautery in the circle of it, as it is turned.
And some wise men say that it should be cauterized with the last cautery in the middle part; but I have not seen this, because I fear it may cause an ulcer, and I have already seen something similar a few times.
And it is more advisable to be cauterized in the circle of it with a circular cautery, as we have said, rather than with a blunt or flat cautery.
Chapter 51.
On the Cauterization of Abscesses.
When some abscess is delayed in its maturity, and this is due to the superfluity of matter within it, or because of the state of the patient, who is old, decrepit, with little blood, or because of the time, and you want to hasten the maturation of the abscess; then cauterize in the circle of it with a small flat cautery, making many small punctures; and then leave that alone, so that it matures quickly.
But if you want the abscess to be perforated with the cautery, then ignite the cautery of which this is the shape, and place that in the middle part of the abscess until the flesh penetrates it.
And if the cautery in that place is left there, because the arm of the patient will be relieved; and then cover that with a dressing until it heals.
Chapter 52.
On the Cauterization of Ulcerating Sores.
Ulceration is a wandering corruption in the limb, which eats away at it like fire consuming dry wood.
Therefore, if you encounter ulceration in a place where the skin is thin and susceptible to burning with hot cautery, then ignite sharp-pointed flat cauteries, small or large as it suits that place where the ulceration is.
And then apply the cautery to that place in its entirety until you eradicate all the corruption and there remains no cause for it.
And then leave that place alone for three days, and apply a salve made with oil mixed with three times its amount of lard over the areas that were cauterized, until all the scabs are eradicated and all corruption is gone.
And then cover that place with a flesh-forming ointment.
But if after three days the flesh that has grown is sound and there is no corruption in it, then it's well. But if not, then you should repeat the cautery over those places where the corruption remains.
And ulceration is medicated with sharp medicine on some occasions, because that is half of cauterization itself. But however, cauterizing with fire is a more gentle remedy overall.
And you have already been told the cure for sharp medicine in its place, and therefore take that when you have developed it.
Chapter 53.
On the Cauterization of Blisters and their Similarities.
Sometimes a large and swollen boil forms on the left side of the foot, which is called a blister, and it causes great pain; and cauterization in those places can be done in two ways, that is, with fire or with hot water.
But the fire method is to ignite the cautery in the form of a scorpion's tail, which is made of iron according to the amount that contains the blister from top to bottom, and with fine edges.
And then place that ignited cautery over the blister, and then turn your hand with the cautery in the circle of the blister until the cautery reaches the depth of the blister. And then leave it alone for three days so that a scab begins to form. And then plaster that area with wild marjoram leaves shredded with salt, and leave the plaster over it for one night, so that the blister is eradicated from its roots.
And then cover the area with a flesh-forming ointment until it heals.
And if it doesn't convert, and it occasionally happens on the surface of the body, mostly on the hands or feet, then take that cautery with water, and do this: take a quill, reed, or scorpion's tail made of horn, iron, or wood, and place that over the blister; then pour a small amount of hot water into the quill, grasp it tightly with your hand, and squeeze the quill until the pressure reaches the root of the blister, and allow the hot water to penetrate the root of the blister for about an hour. Wait patiently for the sting of the hot water to kill the root of the blister, and then remove the quill.
And do it in that way for those who are located elsewhere on the body, until you cover all of them with their roots.
And then cover those areas with the ointment water that will cause flesh to regenerate, once the roots of the blisters have been eradicated.
Chapter 54.
On the Cauterization of Tremors.
When you encounter a tremor due to irritation of the nerves or fever caused by an irritant, or for another similar reason, then it is necessary that you cauterize that area with four cauteries or V-shaped ones on the vertebrae of the back, between each vertebra one cautery; and cauterize the feet as well, and over the belly of the patient, olive-shaped cauteries.
And the patient's tremors cease and hasten the recovery from the illness caused by the irritation.
Chapter 55.
On the Cauterization of Accidental Swellings on the Body.

It seems we've moved on to a new section, describing the treatment for a specific condition affecting the eyelid "dejhos" ( likely meaning "below", as in the lower eyelid). The text is discussing a surgical procedure or remedy for this condition, possibly called "ehacrati".
This eyelid condition, which is called "alxacrati" (likely meaning a type of eyelid drooping or sagging), can be either natural or accidental. In other words, it may be a congenital condition or one that occurs due to some external factor or injury.
The accidental type of alxacrati is caused by injury, such as a blow (plagu), a cut or incision (scissura), or burning with a cautery tool (cauteri) or other similar traumas.
The surgical procedure for treating accidental alxacrati involves using a needle (agula) with doubled thread to make a suture. The needle is inserted into the flesh and passed through both the lacrimal canaliculi, one from the left eye (senestre) to the right eye (dextre), leaving the threads on either side of the skin.
And then, extending the flesh to the upper parts with the needle, tie it off with the thread and incise (or cut) the skin with a spatula, making a wide opening. And thus, if the eyelid returns to its natural shape, it's done. But if not, take a probe and insert it into the slit you made earlier, and use it to shape the lower eyelid back to normal. Then, close the two incisions on the underside of the lower eyelid.
And the ends of the two incisions that you made should be like the two angles of the cut (inscizio) itself, when they come together. And let their joined angle form a figure of its own shape.
And this figure is the Greek letter Lambda (λ).
And then, close up the flesh to the extent that it is the thickness of the lower eyelid itself. In other words, let it be as thick as the normal eyelid.
And then, adjust the separate parts and sew them up with linen thread. And finally, care for it as we have said, using moistening medicines and poultices until it is healed.
And if the alxacrati is caused by a fissure or suture or cauterization, then it's proper to make a flat incision along the skin of the eyelid, following the previous treatment. And then, separate with a poultice (calgua) between two layers (labias), as we have said.

On the cure of hernias.
This disease called a hernia is nothing but a swelling that has been pushed into the inguinal canal, resembling descending water and it is not that.
The method of treating this disease is that you make the patient sit on a prepared and straight chair, and then take hold of his head with both hands and press it into the middle until you see the swelling come down to the lower parts, and then it dries up and does not descend, and thus the light returns to him, and he sees the causes as before.

Of ventilation and the qualities of using those [instruments].
Ventilations are of horns, or of iron, or of wood.
And ventilation is done in two manners: one of them is scarification and extraction of blood, and the other is ventilation without scarification.
And this ventilation that is without scarification is done in two manners, because it is with fire or without fire.
And there are 13 places in the body where ventilation is done with scarification and extraction of blood, from which one place where it is applied is alnocrati, and it is at the back of the head; and the middle part of the neck between the two parts of the collarbone; and below the jawbone just below the mouth; and with spatulas; and alohoster, which is on the end of the pubic bone; and with two needles, and they are 2 inches long; and with two small hooks; and with two crescent-shaped instruments.
And ventilation does not extract blood, but rather from the small and scattered veins in the flesh, and for this reason it does not deplete the vital fluids, as is done with flebotomy; nor should ventilation be done with fire or without fire in any disease caused by a buildup of fluid within the body until all the bodily fluid has been evacuated.
However, if it is necessary, it provokes ventilation for illness or for continuity. Therefore, I administer that [i.e. the treatment] at the beginning of each month and at its end, and also in the middle of it, and sometimes at other times.

And you know that the broken bones in men who are in their first youth and those who are decrepit cannot be continued and consolidated according to their nature because of the dryness of their limbs.
But nature adjusts and connects itself above the broken bone in such a way that it resembles a kind of glue which thickens and adheres to and strengthens that part, which is then conglutinated and joined together, until the end of its fortification and firmness, just as fire at first, until no cause prevents it from completing its work.
And for this reason it is necessary to abstain from feeding the patient foods that are heavy and viscous and gross, just as we have said.

The various kinds of fractures within itself. Signs of bone fracture. And because of this it is known that there is a fracture of the bone: it is the twisting or tortuousness of it, and that prominence and appearance to the sense, and thus when you compress that with your hand.
And therefore, when there is no apparent twisting or deformity and it is not a cause for concern, you should not examine it further when you touch the bone with agitation and the patient does not feel great pain, then it is not here a fracture.
However, it is possible that there is tortuosity or a small fissure, then you should not manipulate it with your hand and with compression of all kinds; but rather pause over it with the medications of which there is reminiscence fitting to this moment, and strictly suitable for its location; and strictly so for subtle strictures.
And you know that the location when it is curved and not split in two or another shape, such as star-shaped, but is re-formed all around its comparison, then it is necessary to start from your time to correct it having had an apostema (a swelling or abscess) occurring to it.

And know that the restoration of him and the stitching of him is much easier than for bones in which such a thing happens.
And apply to it strength according to what will come to mind about him.
But if the fracture is in one of the bones, then it is necessary to make an extension of this broken member from two parts, whether it is the hand or the foot; or with a splint for the hand if the member is small; or with two cords or with one cord and a cloth.
And have your position such that the member is placed in its natural shape while the parts are extended from the broken member; then it is necessary for you to make them return to their places by ingenuity and in whatever manner you can.
And take care, according to your strength, that the operation does not harm or injure the patient; and do your best, according to your power, to place one bone into another so that their joints are aligned in the best possible way.

But Hippocrates does not mention in his book that it should be applied to the broken member for its restoration, but rather mentions cerot, made from wax and oil, and recommends that it should be of medium consistency between hardness and softness.
But Galen sees that it should be applied to the broken member for its restoration and lists among the causes of its effectiveness substances of little quality such as myrrh, resin, and similar substances to those which we have recommended.
Method of ointment that comforts lesions and pain: recipe mixed, from beeswax, human cut-off hairs or bird beak skin, althea, salt, all crushed together; mix well and sifted to make an ointment.
But the quantity that it should have so that the ointment remains and does not separate is such that you consider whether there is no pain or swelling and if the bone is not broken, then it's not good for its place; otherwise you may spend many days in vain. And if it happens that a strong pain, swelling or inflammation occurs at the place, then you remove or take away that thing in an hour and apply the ointment to it.
And take linen and sea sponge, leon's marine sponge, wet it and submerge it in hot water, then immerse that thing into the water and let it wash the place until the swelling ceases and the pain is calmed; and then leave the member to rest for an hour; and then apply a compress soaked in warm wine or oil over the place for one night until you are sure of no boil, and that the inflammation of the member has ceased, and the pain is relieved.
And then gradually apply that gentle stricture and small ointment without tightening too much at first, and gently with it until the member is healed.
And if the boil and pain and swelling and inflammation and all the accidents are completely healed, and you desire ointment and stricture again, then you will repeat that as you did at the beginning in equal measure.
And if no accident occurs in the member of any of those things we have mentioned, then you should not remove it until three or four or five or six days; and sometimes all this is left for twenty days according to how your judgment appears by the separation of the member, as we said, until the fracture adheres and comes close to the coagulation of the flesh over that.
And then you should adjust the stricture to be tighter than your first constriction, and adjust according to the thickening of the flesh of the patient, as it is preceded by the healing of him.
But if the place of the fracture is already dry and exhausted more than it should be, then you know that nourishment is prohibited from reaching it; and therefore, drink hot water with it every time you relieve it; and do this for three days; and loosen the stricture a little, and by this operation, bring nourishment to the member, and it will be healed lightly.
But what the foolish restorers of the fractured member do at another time, when it is not restored at first as it should be, and is restored with difficulty, is an error in their operation, and a great fear; and if they were to write this down, the Ancients would have considered them wrongdoers.
And I have never seen anyone do this before, so it seems reasonable that one should not do it.
Second chapter: Of fractures which happen on the head.
Fractures have various forms and shapes, and distinct causes, for some fractures are caused by the impact of an axe, which crushes the bone entirely into splinters, leaving the splinter behind, just as a wedge does to wood, and this type is called axial; or the axe strikes some part of the bone, and only cuts through the flesh without penetrating further inside.
And the wound of these two fractures is either large or small, and of fracture that is crushing or pressing; its cause is the impact of hammer or weight on rock, and they resemble them.
And this fracture is either penetrating that it approaches the periosteum which is behind the bone; or it is in the face of the bone, and the wound of these two fractures is either large or small.
And of fracture that it is split in the bone, in the subtlety of small hair, and therefore this type of fracture is called capillary.
And this is a fracture that is caused by crushing or impact from rock, and resembles it, which makes some plate of the bone enter into the inner parts, and is done in the place of concavity such as happens to the bones of the ear when they are struck and separated from their entrance into the inner parts.
And it is most commonly done in the hollowed-out bones of small creatures, such as bird skulls.
And in all these severe fractures that are shattered, they are thus separated like stars. And you will come to a recovery from all of this in your place.
And we will observe all these types of fractures by detection above them and by inquiry into their very attempts and outward signs of corrupted flesh that are upon them.
And the special capillary thing is known by this which is discovered over the bone, and it's wiped away, and lint applied to it, because the fracture appears black.

On the restoration of a nose that has been bitten off.
Know that the nose is not torn from one piece but rather two parts joined together very closely, or as it happens occasionally, so that you see two bones in it; because the part behind is cartilaginous and not torn, nor does any damage occur to it, except for the twisting, bending, and sinuosity.

And you should try to restore it to its original state on the first day of the fracture, if possible; and if not, then bring the vinegar or honey to help the rest and recovery from the suppurative wound.

Of the restoration of the fractured ulna (the bone in the forearm).
The ulna is that which is between the elbow and the head of the shoulder.
And if it is broken, then the patient's restoration is in one of two methods, of which one is that you take a plank made from green wood and shape it according to this form:
And attach two wooden strips on the two ends and suspend it in an elevated location.
And follow the patient on a stretcher; and throw their broken arm over the plank so that it reaches the end of it at its midpoint where the curvature of the plank is attached.
And then suspend it above something heavy, or the servant will extend it to its parts; and then the physician should put the broken pieces together in their proper place so that the fracture returns as it should.
And the other method is that the patient be laid on their back and suspend the arm from the hook so that it is stretched out; and then command two servants, one of them should hold what is above the fracture in its place, and the other should hold what is below it; and each of them should stretch it to its part.
And if you want the extension to be stronger, have someone pull the plank with the fracture in it towards them and another person hold the other end of the plank; and each of the servants should stretch it out to its two parts.
And therefore if the fracture is near the end of the muscle, have it so that half of the plank is on the joint and the other half below the fracture, covering it.
And similarly if the fracture is near the tendon, have it so that the plank is placed over that location and over the tendon.
And bind the arm with cloth and bandage it; and have it so that it is bound for as long as needed, and applied in a good manner, lest if you do not take care, an abscess forms.
But if an abscess does form, then leave the bandage off after 7 days and put a linen cloth saturated with vinegar and rose oil over it until the abscess subsides; and then bind it again.

Capítulo XXII parece ser un capítulo de un libro o tratado médico antiguo, específicamente sobre la curación de fracturas óseas. La frase sugiere que, una vez restaurada la forma natural del hueso fracturado, se debe evitar realizar operaciones adicionales en él, ya que esto podría provocar complicaciones.
Cuando se produce una deformidad en el hueso ya restaurado, es adecuado aplicar un proceso de sanación y aplanamiento del hueso fracturado, y también la nodulización. Esto se hace para restaurar la forma correcta del miembro. Sin embargo, a pesar de esta operación adicional, el miembro no debe ser privado de su función natural. Lo importante es que no recibas la palabra de alguien que afirme que ese miembro es nuevo y fracturado, sino que se mantenga confiado en el proceso de restauración y sanación realizado.
Pero ya que he dicho esto, quiero dejar claro que no se debe considerar culpable o condenable a los médicos y restauradores que han realizado esta operación en nuestra tierra; y este procedimiento es digno de miedo, ya que su señal (probablemente una cicatriz) puede ser mortal. La frase sugiere que la herida o cicatriz resultante de la operación puede ser letal si no se trata adecuadamente o si se infecta.
Pero si la claudicación y la nodulización son recientes, entonces es conveniente que sean tratadas con una aplicación de agua tibia en la que se cocinen hierbas suaves para aliviar el dolor, como hojas de aloe, raíces de lu, meliloto, y similares; y debe hacerse un emplaste con una consistencia suave, similar a la diálica bien hecha; o tomar un moco de raíz de aloe y mezclarlo con grasa de gualina o aceite de cedro, y aplicarlo en el área afectada; o usar figuras grasas que se hayan exprimido en huevos de gallina, y que tengan una apariencia similar a las medicinas llamadas consolidadoras. La frase sugiere que el tratamiento debe ser suave y calmante para aliviar el dolor y la inflamación.
Y luego, al cabo de algunas semanas, es disuelta con una ligera fricción y asiduidad, y se administra un movimiento suave y ligero para el miembro afectado, a lo largo de todo el día, en todas las horas. La frase sugiere que el tratamiento debe ser continuo y regular, con movimientos suaves y repetitivos, para ayudar al cuerpo a recuperarse y a la articulación a sanar.
Pero si la deformidad y el hueso se han convertido en una quilla (una pieza dura y aguda) y es necesaria una curación con hierro, entonces ahora es conveniente que se retire el pus infectado y se disuelva la continuación del hueso, y se haga un corte superficial en aquello que sobra de la nodulización de aquel metal (probablemente una cicatriz o una protuberancia) en el hueso con instrumentos afilados, y se administre facilidad en aquel lugar con soluciones y estudios. La frase sugiere que si la deformidad ha llegado a un punto crítico y es necesaria una curación con hierro (probablemente una cirugía), entonces ahora es el momento de retirar el pus infectado, disolver la continuación del hueso y tratar cualquier cicatriz o protuberancia que pueda haber quedado.

Of a sprain or dislocation.

Treatment of dislocation of the jawbone.

And therefore it is not fitting that someone other than a wise and experienced physician with long practice, mercy, and compassion should attempt to treat him; but rather one who is slow, unbold, and modest in the beginning of treatments using medications that will quickly ease swellings, and lessening the patient's suffering to divine judgment, rather to that which you hope for his salvation from peril, from illness alleviation, and in which you see some hope. And then strive to make a reduction from him at the beginning of the cause, before swelling becomes hardened.
And then if the member returns as desired, administer a regimen that will ease hardened swelling and cure the wound with the ointments that are suitable for him.
And if the dislocation is accompanied by a fracture and the bone fragments are separated, then you should perform the reduction of their joint, and do in this case what we have said about simple fractures that occur in those bones.
And keep and avoid, according to your virtue, those who are not prepared in the ways of fear, as you have been preceded by my preaching; for that is better than pleasing yourself, and more permanent to your glory, and brings greater salvation to your true self in their time.
